Remembering what has happened in the past has the power to lift our spirits and give us hope. And thatâ€™s exactly what the Israelites did when they celebrated Passover. The Passover commemorates what God did for the Israelites when they were in Egypt, oppressed by Pharaoh and his crew (Exodus 1:6â€“14). After they cried out to God, He delivered the people in a mighty way. He told them to put blood on their doorposts so the death angel would â€œpass overâ€ their firstborn people and animals (12:12â€“13). Then they would be kept safe from death. SCRIPTURE INSIGHT The point of the first Passover was substitutionary death: a spotless lamb sacrificed in place of the firstborn son. As with all elements of worship prescribed in the Old Testament, this points to the future Messiah who would be the once-for-all sacrifice for the entire human race. At the Passover observance we now know as the Last Supper, Jesus said, â€œThis is my blood of the covenant, which is poured out for many for the forgiveness of sinsâ€ (Matthew 26:28). Part 2 Blood on the Doorposts  Tell the whole community of Israel that on the tenth day of this month each man is to take a lamb for his family, one for each householdâ€¦ Take care of them until the fourteenth day of the month, when all the people of the community of Israel must slaughter them at twilight. Then they are to take some of the blood and put it on the sides and tops of the doorframes of the houses where they eat the lambsâ€¦ The blood will be a sign for you on the houses where you are; and when I see the blood, I will pass over you. No destructive plague will touch you when I strike Egypt. â€“ Exodus 12:3-4, 6-7, 12  What was the significance of putting blood on the doorposts? One very important thing to realize is how it foreshadows the future shedding of blood of Christ, that protects us from judgment, just as the blood here protected the families from judgment.  But yet, the act of putting blood on the doorposts says other things as well. One is that it was a public commitment to the God of Israel in that hostile land, in which that kind of sacrifice was an abomination, which would lead to the personâ€™s being stoned (Ex. 8:26). Only those that were convinced that God would triumph over the Egyptian gods would have done so because of fear of public execution.  Also, putting the blood on the doorposts was a mark of faith that apparently was not limited to Israelites, but anyone who placed his or her faith in God. The text says that many others left Egypt with the Israelites (Ex. 12:38) â€“ perhaps they too had claimed this God by marking their homes. Even some of Pharaohâ€™s officials feared the Lord â€“ could some of them have even done it? Interestingly, entire homes and families were saved, just as in the New Testament, entire families were baptized and saved (Acts 16:34). Even Rahab the harlot was able to save her family by marking her home with a scarlet cord! (Josh. 6:25) The Bible often talks about salvation in terms of families, while we think in terms of individuals.  Finally, it is amazing that God told people to make a sacrifice and put the blood on their homes. Normally sacrifices were made at an altar in a tabernacle or temple, and only the ceremonially clean could enter in. Godâ€™s great shekinah glory would be very present at the altar, apart from the rest of the people. Here, God was telling them to anoint their home as Godâ€™s altar, and publically place their faith in him. Godâ€™s presence came that night and to those who did not fear him, it lead to judgment. But to those who had faith, it would set them free.

I like how real and relatable this song is. While the song seems about empowerment, it also portrays the fear of vulnerability in some people and why they do. We often put on a tough exterior to hide our insecurities. We don't want others to know what these flaws are because we know how cruel some people can be to those who are weak and we have been too traumatized with their brutal invalidation of our struggles. I'm not saying this is bad but we shouldn't shut our hearts for too long. We may not realize the dangers of wearing this mask for a long time but it is indeed exhausting, and if it becomes too much, it overtires you to the point of collapsing. It wrecks us in the long run. Saying "I'm unstoppable" is how some of us empower and motivate ourselves and that is great. But also being able to show our vulnerable side and accepting help from others will make us a lot stronger and freer.

Love
The music video has a lot to say.   The girl at first prepares for impact. The reason for her to wear bulky trousers, to show that, no matter what burden is there, they will fight.  Then she after breaking some more glasses looks at a drawing. The drawing was done in a very old time. The girl looking at old painting shows and the lyrics "I don't need batteries", suggests  that  people who are unstoppable, don't need a constant source of motivation, because if your goals are strong enough, you'll do it, even if the odds are not in your favour. And, you are like a matchstick, a small spark and you can light anything. But then after breaking few more obstacles, the girl comes across a glass. She goes near the glass, indicating that the glass is stronger than previous, and using her old methods won't satisfy her. She then licks the glass indicating that, she has put a mark on the obstacle, and she will prepapre for a newer method to break the glass. She does find a newer method, and breaks the glass. And, the reason she was jumping indicates her actions that involved- not stopping at that point, and challenging herself to fight with more.  The people keep bringing obstacles, because without them, we can never know who is stoppable and who is not Ultimately, the whole video goes with breaking obstacles with no ending.  The video can have many meanings to different people, This was the meaning I learnt at first  So, the moral we learned is " Everyone is Stoppable, but unstoppable are those, who even after stopping do not give up"  And....sorry for the Bad English :')
